164 "About four in the afternoon, being no longer able to contain my"
164 "impatience, I went to the central staircase.  The panel was open, and I"
164 "ventured on to the platform.  The Captain was still walking up and down"
164 "with an agitated step.  He was looking at the ship, which was five or"
164 "six miles to leeward."
164 ""
164 "He was going round it like a wild beast, and, drawing it eastward, he"
164 "allowed them to pursue.  But he did not attack.  Perhaps he still"
164 "hesitated?  I wished to mediate once more.  But I had scarcely spoken,"
164 "when Captain Nemo imposed silence, saying:"
164 ""
164 "\"I am the law, and I am the judge!  I am the oppressed, and there is"
164 "the oppressor!  Through him I have lost all that I loved, cherished,"
164 "and venerated--country, wife, children, father, and mother.  I saw all"
164 "perish!  All that I hate is there!  Say no more!\""
164 ""
164 "I cast a last look at the man-of-war, which was putting on steam, and"
164 "rejoined Ned and Conseil."
164 ""
164 "\"We will fly!\"  I exclaimed."
164 ""
164 "\"Good!\" said Ned.  \"What is this vessel?\""
164 ""
164 "\"I do not know; but, whatever it is, it will be sunk before night.  In"
164 "any case, it is better to perish with it, than be made accomplices in a"
164 "retaliation the justice of which we cannot judge.\""
164 ""
164 "\"That is my opinion too,\" said Ned Land, coolly.  \"Let us wait for"
164 "night.\""
164 ""
164 "Night arrived.  Deep silence reigned on board.  The compass showed that"
164 "the Nautilus had not altered its course.  It was on the surface,"
164 "rolling slightly.  My companions and I resolved to fly when the vessel"
164 "should be near enough either to hear us or to see us; for the moon,"
164 "which would be full in two or three days, shone brightly.  Once on"
164 "board the ship, if we could not prevent the blow which threatened it,"
164 "we could, at least we would, do all that circumstances would allow."
164 "Several times I thought the Nautilus was preparing for attack; but"
164 "Captain Nemo contented himself with allowing his adversary to approach,"
164 "and then fled once more before it."
164 ""
164 "Part of the night passed without any incident.  We watched the"
164 "opportunity for action.  We spoke little, for we were too much moved."
164 "Ned Land would have thrown himself into the sea, but I forced him to"
164 "wait.  According to my idea, the Nautilus would attack the ship at her"
164 "waterline, and then it would not only be possible, but easy to fly."
164 ""
164 "At three in the morning, full of uneasiness, I mounted the platform."
164 "Captain Nemo had not left it.  He was standing at the fore part near"
164 "his flag, which a slight breeze displayed above his head.  He did not"
164 "take his eyes from the vessel.  The intensity of his look seemed to"
164 "attract, and fascinate, and draw it onward more surely than if he had"
164 "been towing it.  The moon was then passing the meridian.  Jupiter was"
164 "rising in the east.  Amid this peaceful scene of nature, sky and ocean"
164 "rivalled each other in tranquillity, the sea offering to the orbs of"
164 "night the finest mirror they could ever have in which to reflect their"
164 "image.  As I thought of the deep calm of these elements, compared with"
164 "all those passions brooding imperceptibly within the Nautilus, I"
164 "shuddered."
164 ""
164 "The vessel was within two miles of us.  It was ever nearing that"
164 "phosphorescent light which showed the presence of the Nautilus.  I"
164 "could see its green and red lights, and its white lantern hanging from"
164 "the large foremast.  An indistinct vibration quivered through its"
164 "rigging, showing that the furnaces were heated to the uttermost."
164 "Sheaves of sparks and red ashes flew from the funnels, shining in the"
164 "atmosphere like stars."
164 ""
164 "I remained thus until six in the morning, without Captain Nemo noticing"
164 "me.  The ship stood about a mile and a half from us, and with the first"
164 "dawn of day the firing began afresh.  The moment could not be far off"
164 "when, the Nautilus attacking its adversary, my companions and myself"
164 "should for ever leave this man.  I was preparing to go down to remind"
164 "them, when the second mounted the platform, accompanied by several"
164 "sailors.  Captain Nemo either did not or would not see them.  Some"
164 "steps were taken which might be called the signal for action.  They"
164 "were very simple.  The iron balustrade around the platform was lowered,"
164 "and the lantern and pilot cages were pushed within the shell until they"
164 "were flush with the deck.  The long surface of the steel cigar no"
164 "longer offered a single point to check its manoeuvres.  I returned to"
164 "the saloon.  The Nautilus still floated; some streaks of light were"
164 "filtering through the liquid beds.  With the undulations of the waves"
164 "the windows were brightened by the red streaks of the rising sun, and"
164 "this dreadful day of the 2nd of June had dawned."
164 ""
164 "At five o'clock, the log showed that the speed of the Nautilus was"
164 "slackening, and I knew that it was allowing them to draw nearer."
164 "Besides, the reports were heard more distinctly, and the projectiles,"
164 "labouring through the ambient water, were extinguished with a strange"
164 "hissing noise."
164 ""
164 "\"My friends,\" said I, \"the moment is come.  One grasp of the hand, and"
164 "may God protect us!\""
164 ""
164 "Ned Land was resolute, Conseil calm, myself so nervous that I knew not"
164 "how to contain myself.  We all passed into the library; but the moment"
164 "I pushed the door opening on to the central staircase, I heard the"
164 "upper panel close sharply.  The Canadian rushed on to the stairs, but I"
164 "stopped him.  A well-known hissing noise told me that the water was"
164 "running into the reservoirs, and in a few minutes the Nautilus was some"
164 "yards beneath the surface of the waves.  I understood the manoeuvre."
164 "It was too late to act.  The Nautilus did not wish to strike at the"
164 "impenetrable cuirass, but below the water-line, where the metallic"
164 "covering no longer protected it."
164 ""
164 "We were again imprisoned, unwilling witnesses of the dreadful drama"
164 "that was preparing.  We had scarcely time to reflect; taking refuge in"
164 "my room, we looked at each other without speaking.  A deep stupor had"
164 "taken hold of my mind:  thought seemed to stand still.  I was in that"
164 "painful state of expectation preceding a dreadful report.  I waited, I"
164 "listened, every sense was merged in that of hearing!  The speed of the"
164 "Nautilus was accelerated.  It was preparing to rush.  The whole ship"
164 "trembled.  Suddenly I screamed.  I felt the shock, but comparatively"
164 "light.  I felt the penetrating power of the steel spur.  I heard"
164 "rattlings and scrapings.  But the Nautilus, carried along by its"
164 "propelling power, passed through the mass of the vessel like a needle"
164 "through sailcloth!"
164 ""
164 "I could stand it no longer.  Mad, out of my mind, I rushed from my room"
164 "into the saloon.  Captain Nemo was there, mute, gloomy, implacable; he"
164 "was looking through the port panel.  A large mass cast a shadow on the"
164 "water; and, that it might lose nothing of her agony, the Nautilus was"
164 "going down into the abyss with her.  Ten yards from me I saw the open"
164 "shell, through which the water was rushing with the noise of thunder,"
164 "then the double line of guns and the netting.  The bridge was covered"
164 "with black, agitated shadows."
164 ""
164 "The water was rising.  The poor creatures were crowding the ratlines,"
164 "clinging to the masts, struggling under the water.  It was a human"
164 "ant-heap overtaken by the sea.  Paralysed, stiffened with anguish, my"
164 "hair standing on end, with eyes wide open, panting, without breath, and"
164 "without voice, I too was watching!  An irresistible attraction glued me"
164 "to the glass!  Suddenly an explosion took place.  The compressed air"
164 "blew up her decks, as if the magazines had caught fire.  Then the"
164 "unfortunate vessel sank more rapidly.  Her topmast, laden with victims,"
164 "now appeared; then her spars, bending under the weight of men; and,"
164 "last of all, the top of her mainmast.  Then the dark mass disappeared,"
164 "and with it the dead crew, drawn down by the strong eddy."
164 ""
164 "I turned to Captain Nemo.  That terrible avenger, a perfect archangel"
164 "of hatred, was still looking.  When all was over, he turned to his"
164 "room, opened the door, and entered.  I followed him with my eyes.  On"
164 "the end wall beneath his heroes, I saw the portrait of a woman, still"
164 "young, and two little children.  Captain Nemo looked at them for some"
164 "moments, stretched his arms towards them, and, kneeling down, burst"
164 "into deep sobs."
164 ""
164 ""
164 ""
164 "CHAPTER XXII"
164 ""
164 "THE LAST WORDS OF CAPTAIN NEMO"
164 ""
164 "The panels had closed on this dreadful vision, but light had not"
164 "returned to the saloon:  all was silence and darkness within the"
164 "Nautilus.  At wonderful speed, a hundred feet beneath the water, it was"
164 "leaving this desolate spot.  Whither was it going?  To the north or"
164 "south?  Where was the man flying to after such dreadful retaliation?  I"
164 "had returned to my room, where Ned and Conseil had remained silent"
164 "enough.  I felt an insurmountable horror for Captain Nemo.  Whatever he"
164 "had suffered at the hands of these men, he had no right to punish thus."
164 "He had made me, if not an accomplice, at least a witness of his"
164 "vengeance.  At eleven the electric light reappeared.  I passed into the"
164 "saloon.  It was deserted.  I consulted the different instruments.  The"
164 "Nautilus was flying northward at the rate of twenty-five miles an hour,"
164 "now on the surface, and now thirty feet below it.  On taking the"
164 "bearings by the chart, I saw that we were passing the mouth of the"
164 "Manche, and that our course was hurrying us towards the northern seas"
164 "at a frightful speed.  That night we had crossed two hundred leagues of"
164 "the Atlantic.  The shadows fell, and the sea was covered with darkness"
164 "until the rising of the moon.  I went to my room, but could not sleep."
164 "I was troubled with dreadful nightmare.  The horrible scene of"
164 "destruction was continually before my eyes.  From that day, who could"
164 "tell into what part of the North Atlantic basin the Nautilus would take"
164 "us?  Still with unaccountable speed.  Still in the midst of these"
164 "northern fogs.  Would it touch at Spitzbergen, or on the shores of Nova"
164 "Zembla?  Should we explore those unknown seas, the White Sea, the Sea"
164 "of Kara, the Gulf of Obi, the Archipelago of Liarrov, and the unknown"
164 "coast of Asia?  I could not say.  I could no longer judge of the time"
164 "that was passing.  The clocks had been stopped on board.  It seemed, as"
164 "in polar countries, that night and day no longer followed their regular"
164 "course.  I felt myself being drawn into that strange region where the"
164 "foundered imagination of Edgar Poe roamed at will.  Like the fabulous"
164 "Gordon Pym, at every moment I expected to see \"that veiled human"
164 "figure, of larger proportions than those of any inhabitant of the"
164 "earth, thrown across the cataract which defends the approach to the"
164 "pole.\" I estimated (though, perhaps, I may be mistaken)--I estimated"
164 "this adventurous course of the Nautilus to have lasted fifteen or"
164 "twenty days.  And I know not how much longer it might have lasted, had"
164 "it not been for the catastrophe which ended this voyage.  Of Captain"
164 "Nemo I saw nothing whatever now, nor of his second.  Not a man of the"
164 "crew was visible for an instant.  The Nautilus was almost incessantly"
164 "under water.  When we came to the surface to renew the air, the panels"
164 "opened and shut mechanically.  There were no more marks on the"
164 "planisphere.  I knew not where we were.  And the Canadian, too, his"
164 "strength and patience at an end, appeared no more.  Conseil could not"
164 "draw a word from him; and, fearing that, in a dreadful fit of madness,"
164 "he might kill himself, watched him with constant devotion.  One morning"
164 "(what date it was I could not say) I had fallen into a heavy sleep"
164 "towards the early hours, a sleep both painful and unhealthy, when I"
164 "suddenly awoke.  Ned Land was leaning over me, saying, in a low voice,"
164 "\"We are going to fly.\"  I sat up."
164 ""
164 "\"When shall we go?\"  I asked."
164 ""
164 "\"To-night. All inspection on board the Nautilus seems to have ceased."
164 "All appear to be stupefied.  You will be ready, sir?\""
164 ""
164 "\"Yes; where are we?\""
164 ""
164 "\"In sight of land.  I took the reckoning this morning in the"
164 "fog--twenty miles to the east.\""
164 ""
164 "\"What country is it?\""
164 ""
164 "\"I do not know; but, whatever it is, we will take refuge there.\""
164 ""
164 "\"Yes, Ned, yes.  We will fly to-night, even if the sea should swallow"
164 "us up.\""
164 ""
164 "\"The sea is bad, the wind violent, but twenty miles in that light boat"
164 "of the Nautilus does not frighten me.  Unknown to the crew, I have been"
164 "able to procure food and some bottles of water.\""
164 ""
164 "\"I will follow you.\""
164 ""
164 "\"But,\" continued the Canadian, \"if I am surprised, I will defend"
164 "myself; I will force them to kill me.\""
164 ""
164 "\"We will die together, friend Ned.\""
164 ""
164 "I had made up my mind to all.  The Canadian left me.  I reached the"
164 "platform, on which I could with difficulty support myself against the"
164 "shock of the waves.  The sky was threatening; but, as land was in those"
164 "thick brown shadows, we must fly.  I returned to the saloon, fearing"
164 "and yet hoping to see Captain Nemo, wishing and yet not wishing to see"
164 "him.  What could I have said to him?  Could I hide the involuntary"
164 "horror with which he inspired me?  No. It was better that I should not"
164 "meet him face to face; better to forget him.  And yet----  How long"
164 "seemed that day, the last that I should pass in the Nautilus.  I"
164 "remained alone.  Ned Land and Conseil avoided speaking, for fear of"
164 "betraying themselves.  At six I dined, but I was not hungry; I forced"
164 "myself to eat in spite of my disgust, that I might not weaken myself."
164 "At half-past six Ned Land came to my room, saying, \"We shall not see"
164 "each other again before our departure.  At ten the moon will not be"
164 "risen.  We will profit by the darkness.  Come to the boat; Conseil and"
164 "I will wait for you.\""
164 ""
164 "The Canadian went out without giving me time to answer.  Wishing to"
164 "verify the course of the Nautilus, I went to the saloon.  We were"
164 "running N.N.E. at frightful speed, and more than fifty yards deep.  I"
164 "cast a last look on these wonders of nature, on the riches of art"
164 "heaped up in this museum, upon the unrivalled collection destined to"
164 "perish at the bottom of the sea, with him who had formed it.  I wished"
164 "to fix an indelible impression of it in my mind.  I remained an hour"
164 "thus, bathed in the light of that luminous ceiling, and passing in"
164 "review those treasures shining under their glasses.  Then I returned to"
164 "my room."
164 ""
164 "I dressed myself in strong sea clothing.  I collected my notes, placing"
164 "them carefully about me.  My heart beat loudly.  I could not check its"
164 "pulsations.  Certainly my trouble and agitation would have betrayed me"
164 "to Captain Nemo's eyes.  What was he doing at this moment?  I listened"
164 "at the door of his room.  I heard steps.  Captain Nemo was there.  He"
164 "had not gone to rest.  At every moment I expected to see him appear,"
164 "and ask me why I wished to fly.  I was constantly on the alert.  My"
164 "imagination magnified everything.  The impression became at last so"
164 "poignant that I asked myself if it would not be better to go to the"
164 "Captain's room, see him face to face, and brave him with look and"
164 "gesture."
164 ""
164 "It was the inspiration of a madman; fortunately I resisted the desire,"
164 "and stretched myself on my bed to quiet my bodily agitation.  My nerves"
164 "were somewhat calmer, but in my excited brain I saw over again all my"
164 "existence on board the Nautilus; every incident, either happy or"
164 "unfortunate, which had happened since my disappearance from the Abraham"
164 "Lincoln--the submarine hunt, the Torres Straits, the savages of Papua,"
164 "the running ashore, the coral cemetery, the passage of Suez, the Island"
164 "of Santorin, the Cretan diver, Vigo Bay, Atlantis, the iceberg, the"
164 "South Pole, the imprisonment in the ice, the fight among the poulps,"
164 "the storm in the Gulf Stream, the Avenger, and the horrible scene of"
164 "the vessel sunk with all her crew.  All these events passed before my"
164 "eyes like scenes in a drama.  Then Captain Nemo seemed to grow"
164 "enormously, his features to assume superhuman proportions.  He was no"
164 "longer my equal, but a man of the waters, the genie of the sea."
164 ""
164 "It was then half-past nine.  I held my head between my hands to keep it"
164 "from bursting.  I closed my eyes; I would not think any longer.  There"
164 "was another half-hour to wait, another half-hour of a nightmare, which"
164 "might drive me mad."
164 ""
164 "At that moment I heard the distant strains of the organ, a sad harmony"
164 "to an undefinable chant, the wail of a soul longing to break these"
164 "earthly bonds.  I listened with every sense, scarcely breathing;"
164 "plunged, like Captain Nemo, in that musical ecstasy, which was drawing"
164 "him in spirit to the end of life."
164 ""
164 "Then a sudden thought terrified me.  Captain Nemo had left his room."
164 "He was in the saloon, which I must cross to fly.  There I should meet"
164 "him for the last time.  He would see me, perhaps speak to me.  A"
164 "gesture of his might destroy me, a single word chain me on board."
164 ""
164 "But ten was about to strike.  The moment had come for me to leave my"
164 "room, and join my companions."
164 ""
164 "I must not hesitate, even if Captain Nemo himself should rise before"
164 "me.  I opened my door carefully; and even then, as it turned on its"
164 "hinges, it seemed to me to make a dreadful noise.  Perhaps it only"
164 "existed in my own imagination."
164 ""
164 "I crept along the dark stairs of the Nautilus, stopping at each step to"
164 "check the beating of my heart.  I reached the door of the saloon, and"
164 "opened it gently.  It was plunged in profound darkness.  The strains of"
164 "the organ sounded faintly.  Captain Nemo was there.  He did not see me."
164 "In the full light I do not think he would have noticed me, so entirely"
164 "was he absorbed in the ecstasy."
164 ""
164 "I crept along the carpet, avoiding the slightest sound which might"
164 "betray my presence.  I was at least five minutes reaching the door, at"
164 "the opposite side, opening into the library."
164 ""
164 "I was going to open it, when a sigh from Captain Nemo nailed me to the"
164 "spot.  I knew that he was rising.  I could even see him, for the light"
164 "from the library came through to the saloon.  He came towards me"
164 "silently, with his arms crossed, gliding like a spectre rather than"
164 "walking.  His breast was swelling with sobs; and I heard him murmur"
164 "these words (the last which ever struck my ear):"
164 ""
164 "\"Almighty God! enough! enough!\""
164 ""
164 "Was it a confession of remorse which thus escaped from this man's"
164 "conscience?"
164 ""
164 "In desperation, I rushed through the library, mounted the central"
164 "staircase, and, following the upper flight, reached the boat.  I crept"
164 "through the opening, which had already admitted my two companions."
164 ""
164 "\"Let us go! let us go!\"  I exclaimed."
164 ""
164 "\"Directly!\" replied the Canadian."
164 ""
164 "The orifice in the plates of the Nautilus was first closed, and"
164 "fastened down by means of a false key, with which Ned Land had provided"
164 "himself; the opening in the boat was also closed.  The Canadian began"
164 "to loosen the bolts which still held us to the submarine boat."
164 ""
164 "Suddenly a noise was heard.  Voices were answering each other loudly."
164 "What was the matter?  Had they discovered our flight?  I felt Ned Land"
164 "slipping a dagger into my hand."
164 ""
164 "\"Yes,\" I murmured, \"we know how to die!\""
164 ""
164 "The Canadian had stopped in his work.  But one word many times"
164 "repeated, a dreadful word, revealed the cause of the agitation"
164 "spreading on board the Nautilus.  It was not we the crew were looking"
164 "after!"
164 ""
164 "\"The maelstrom! the maelstrom!\"  Could a more dreadful word in a more"
164 "dreadful situation have sounded in our ears!  We were then upon the"
164 "dangerous coast of Norway.  Was the Nautilus being drawn into this gulf"
164 "at the moment our boat was going to leave its sides?  We knew that at"
164 "the tide the pent-up waters between the islands of Ferroe and Loffoden"
164 "rush with irresistible violence, forming a whirlpool from which no"
164 "vessel ever escapes.  From every point of the horizon enormous waves"
164 "were meeting, forming a gulf justly called the \"Navel of the Ocean,\""
164 "whose power of attraction extends to a distance of twelve miles."
164 "There, not only vessels, but whales are sacrificed, as well as white"
164 "bears from the northern regions."
164 ""
164 "It is thither that the Nautilus, voluntarily or involuntarily, had been"
164 "run by the Captain."
164 ""
164 "It was describing a spiral, the circumference of which was lessening by"
164 "degrees, and the boat, which was still fastened to its side, was"
164 "carried along with giddy speed.  I felt that sickly giddiness which"
164 "arises from long-continued whirling round."
164 ""
164 "We were in dread.  Our horror was at its height, circulation had"
164 "stopped, all nervous influence was annihilated, and we were covered"
164 "with cold sweat, like a sweat of agony!  And what noise around our"
164 "frail bark!  What roarings repeated by the echo miles away!  What an"
164 "uproar was that of the waters broken on the sharp rocks at the bottom,"
164 "where the hardest bodies are crushed, and trees worn away, \"with all"
164 "the fur rubbed off,\" according to the Norwegian phrase!"
164 ""
164 "What a situation to be in!  We rocked frightfully.  The Nautilus"
164 "defended itself like a human being.  Its steel muscles cracked."
164 "Sometimes it seemed to stand upright, and we with it!"
164 ""
164 "\"We must hold on,\" said Ned, \"and look after the bolts.  We may still"
164 "be saved if we stick to the Nautilus.\""
164 ""
164 "He had not finished the words, when we heard a crashing noise, the"
164 "bolts gave way, and the boat, torn from its groove, was hurled like a"
164 "stone from a sling into the midst of the whirlpool."
164 ""
164 "My head struck on a piece of iron, and with the violent shock I lost"
164 "all consciousness."
164 ""
164 ""
164 ""
164 "CHAPTER XXIII"
164 ""
164 "CONCLUSION"
164 ""
164 "Thus ends the voyage under the seas.  What passed during that"
164 "night--how the boat escaped from the eddies of the maelstrom--how Ned"
164 "Land, Conseil, and myself ever came out of the gulf, I cannot tell."
164 ""
164 "But when I returned to consciousness, I was lying in a fisherman's hut,"
164 "on the Loffoden Isles.  My two companions, safe and sound, were near me"
164 "holding my hands.  We embraced each other heartily."
164 ""
164 "At that moment we could not think of returning to France.  The means of"
164 "communication between the north of Norway and the south are rare.  And"
164 "I am therefore obliged to wait for the steamboat running monthly from"
164 "Cape North."
164 ""
164 "And, among the worthy people who have so kindly received us, I revise"
164 "my record of these adventures once more.  Not a fact has been omitted,"
164 "not a detail exaggerated.  It is a faithful narrative of this"
164 "incredible expedition in an element inaccessible to man, but to which"
164 "Progress will one day open a road."
164 ""
164 "Shall I be believed?  I do not know.  And it matters little, after all."
164 "What I now affirm is, that I have a right to speak of these seas, under"
164 "which, in less than ten months, I have crossed 20,000 leagues in that"
164 "submarine tour of the world, which has revealed so many wonders."
164 ""
164 "But what has become of the Nautilus?  Did it resist the pressure of the"
164 "maelstrom?  Does Captain Nemo still live?  And does he still follow"
164 "under the ocean those frightful retaliations?  Or, did he stop after"
164 "the last hecatomb?"
164 ""
164 "Will the waves one day carry to him this manuscript containing the"
164 "history of his life?  Shall I ever know the name of this man?  Will the"
164 "missing vessel tell us by its nationality that of Captain Nemo?"
164 ""
164 "I hope so.  And I also hope that his powerful vessel has conquered the"
164 "sea at its most terrible gulf, and that the Nautilus has survived where"
164 "so many other vessels have been lost!  If it be so--if Captain Nemo"
164 "still inhabits the ocean, his adopted country, may hatred be appeased"
164 "in that savage heart!  May the contemplation of so many wonders"
164 "extinguish for ever the spirit of vengeance!  May the judge disappear,"
164 "and the philosopher continue the peaceful exploration of the sea!  If"
164 "his destiny be strange, it is also sublime.  Have I not understood it"
164 "myself?  Have I not lived ten months of this unnatural life?  And to"
164 "the question asked by Ecclesiastes three thousand years ago, \"That"
164 "which is far off and exceeding deep, who can find it out?\" two men"
164 "alone of all now living have the right to give an answer----"
164 ""
164 "CAPTAIN NEMO AND MYSELF."
